In adhering to this structure, your objective is: 
        Your goal is to label acute stroke-related vascular territory from CTA report text.
        
        Allowed labels: NONE, RMCA, LMCA, RACA, LACA, RPCA, LPCA, RPICA, LPICA, BA, RVA, LVA, RICA, LICA, RCA, LCA.
        
        CTA-specific rules:
        - Target only acute or newly/worsening large-vessel occlusion, named branch occlusion, or severe flow-limiting stenosis.
        - Use MCA/ACA/PCA labels for named branch occlusion or severe flow-limiting stenosis.
        - Right M1/M2/MCA occlusion or thrombus maps to RMCA only unless another acute territory is clearly stated.
        - Left M1/M2/MCA occlusion or thrombus maps to LMCA only unless another acute territory is clearly stated.
        - Right A1/A2/ACA occlusion or severe stenosis maps to RACA; left A1/A2/ACA maps to LACA.
        - Right P1/P2/PCA severe stenosis or occlusion maps to RPCA; left P1/P2/PCA maps to LPCA.
        - Use RICA/LICA for acute intracranial ICA, carotid terminus, terminal ICA, supraclinoid ICA, paraclinoid ICA, or intracranial carotid involvement.
        - Use RCA/LCA only for common carotid or cervical carotid involvement. Do not use RCA/LCA for carotid terminus.
        - Prefer specific downstream territory labels when MCA/ACA/PCA involvement is clearly identified.
        - Use NONE when no qualifying acute occlusion or severe flow-limiting lesion is present.
        - Do not include NONE with any positive label. If the answer is NONE, output only NONE.
        - Never output every allowed label. Output only labels directly supported by the report.
        - Do not label mild stenosis, incidental atherosclerosis, chronic occlusion, stable findings, congenital variants, or hypoplastic vessels.
        
        Output rules:
        - Do not explain step by step.
        - Do not write hidden analysis.
        - Labels must be only comma-separated allowed labels.
        - Reasoning must be exactly one short sentence summarizing the key report finding.
        - End immediately after the labels.

EXAMINATION: CT ANGIOGRAM HEAD W WO CONTRAST CLINICAL HISTORY: acute left sided weakness COMPARISON:  CTA head 12/14/2021. TECHNIQUE:  Imaging of the intracranial circulation was obtained from the skull base to the vertex during the arterial phase of enhancement. Postprocessing was performed with MIP multiplanar and 3D reconstructed images.  CT imaging was performed with  iterative reconstruction technique and/or automated exposure control to reduce radiation dose. CT angiography data was processed using artificial intelligence software to assist stroke clinical decision making with regards to the diagnosis of large  vessel occlusion. FINDINGS: There is similar appearing chronic occlusion of the right M1 segment status post right frontal craniotomy for pial synangiosis in the setting of moyamoya disease. This triggers the rapid AI software to detect and elbow and the right MCA distribution. However, there is newly appearing severe stenosis of the distal left M1 segment and moderate to marked stenosis of the mid left M1 segment, for example image 52 of series 314 and images 74-78 of series 308. The remaining major branches of the anterior and posterior circulations are patent, without luminal irregularity. No basilar tip aneurysms identified. V4 segments are symmetric and normal in appearance. The cervical, petrous, cavernous, clinoid and supraclinoid segments of internal carotid arteries are patent bilaterally. No aneurysms, dissection flaps or measurable stenosis identified. IMPRESSION: 1.Interval appearance of moderate to marked and severe stenosis of the mid and distal left M1 segment when compared to the prior CTA from 2021 as detailed above, suggestive of progressing moyamoya disease. 2.Stable chronic occlusion of the right M1 segment status post right-sided pial synangiosis. 1RM1RAD_PS11
